The extraction is done once and reused in both places.\\n  - New `recoverToolCallsFromText()` parser in `ollama-stream.ts` extracts structured tool calls from `` XML tags only (fenced JSON code blocks are intentionally excluded per security review). Recovered markup is stripped from text content to prevent history pollution.\\n- What did NOT change (scope boundary): Cloud provider paths, existing `contextWindow` behavior when explicitly set, tool schema generation, the OpenAI-completions/responses tool-call parsing, and fenced JSON code blocks are never interpreted as tool calls.\\n\\n## Change Type (select all)\\n\\n- [x] Bug fix\\n- [ ] Feature\\n- [ ] Refactor\\n- [ ] Docs\\n- [ ] Security hardening\\n- [ ] Chore/infra\\n\\n## Scope (select all touched areas)\\n\\n- [x] Gateway / orchestration\\n- [x] Skills / tool execution\\n- [ ] Auth / tokens\\n- [ ] Memory / storage\\n- [x] Integrations\\n- [x] API / contracts\\n- [ ] UI / DX\\n- [ ] CI/CD / infra\\n\\n## Linked Issue/PR\\n\\n- Closes #50894\\n- Supersedes #51094 (closed — addressed all bot review feedback from that PR)\\n\\n## User-visible / Behavior Changes\\n\\n1. The `options` field is properly propagated through model resolution (previously dropped by `applyConfiguredProviderOverrides`).\\n3. When `contextWindow` is not set but `options.num_ctx` is, the value is used as context window size — preventing silent conversation history truncation.\\n4. Smaller local models that emit `{\\u0026#34;name\\u0026#34;:\\u0026#34;write_file\\u0026#34;,...}` in text output now have those calls recovered and dispatched. Blocking handlers are awaited sequentially and can return `{ cancel, blockReason, replyText }` to abort dispatch and optionally send a rejection reply.\\n- **What did NOT change (scope boundary):** Default observer behavior is preserved. No changes to other hooks, no new global config, no `before_dispatch` hook, no inbound content mutation.\\n\\n## Change Type (select all)\\n\\n- [ ] Bug fix\\n- [x] Feature\\n- [ ] Refactor required for the fix\\n- [ ] Docs\\n- [ ] Security hardening\\n- [ ] Chore/infra\\n\\n## Scope (select all touched areas)\\n\\n- [x] Gateway / orchestration\\n- [ ] Skills / tool execution\\n- [ ] Auth / tokens\\n- [ ] Memory / storage\\n- [x] Integrations\\n- [x] API / contracts\\n- [ ] UI / DX\\n- [ ] CI/CD / infra\\n\\n## Linked Issue/PR\\n\\n- Closes #53341\\n\\n## User-visible / Behavior Changes\\n\\n- Plugin developers can now register `message_received` hooks with `{ mode: \\u0026#34;blocking\\u0026#34; }` to perform async inbound checks before agent dispatch.\\n- Blocking hooks can return `{ cancel: true, replyText: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34; }` to abort processing and send a rejection reply.\\n- No behavior change for existing plugins — default mode remains observer (fire-and-forget).\\n\\n## Security Impact (required)\\n\\n- New permissions/capabilities? `Yes` — blocking hooks can now cancel inbound messages and send rejection replies. For example, an agent\\nsending an Adaptive Card via the `send` tool in a 1:1 chat could have that card appear in a\\nteam channel instead.\\n\\n### Root cause\\n\\nFor DMs, the inbound context sets `To` as `user:{aadObjectId}`. When the `send` tool later\\nresolves the target via `resolveMSTeamsSendContext`, it calls `findByUserId` in the conversation\\nstore, which iterates all stored conversations and returns the **first** entry matching the\\nuser\\u0026#39;s AAD object ID or Bot Framework ID — with no awareness of conversation type or recency.\\n\\nSince `Object.entries()` iteration order depends on insertion order in the JSON store, the\\nresult is non-deterministic from the user\\u0026#39;s perspective: if the channel/group conversation\\nwas stored before the personal DM, the proactive message is delivered there instead.\\n\\nBoth the filesystem store (`conversation-store-fs.ts`) and the in-memory store\\n(`conversation-store-memory.ts`) share this behavior.\\n\\n## Solution\\n\\nUpdate `findByUserId` in both store implementations to collect **all** matching entries for a\\nuser, then apply a preference:\\n\\n1. **Prefer `personal` (1:1) conversations** — when a user lookup is performed (typically for\\n   DM-initiated proactive sends), the personal conversation is the semantically correct target.\\n2. **Fall back deterministically** — when no personal conversation exists, the fs store returns\\n   the most recently seen entry (by `lastSeenAt` timestamp, which already exists in the\\n   persisted data), and the memory store returns the first match.\\n\\nThis approach was chosen over changing the `To` format (Option 2 in the issue) or threading\\nsession context (Option 3/4) because:\\n\\n- It fixes the bug at the source (`findByUserId`) without changing the inbound context format,\\n  avoiding downstream breakage in code paths that parse `user:` prefix for DM detection.\\n- It leverages the `conversationType` field already stored in every conversation reference.\\n- It fixes **all** callers of `findByUserId`, not just the DM inbound path.\\n- The `lastSeenAt` field already exists in the fs store data, so no schema changes are needed.\\n\\n## Changed files\\n\\n| File | Change |\\n|------|--------|\\n| `extensions/msteams/src/conversation-store-fs.ts` | `findByUserId` collects all matches, prefers `personal`, falls back to most recent |\\n| For example, an agent\\nsending an Adaptive Card via the `send` tool in a 1:1 chat could have that card appear in a\\nteam channel instead.\\n\\n### Root cause\\n\\nFor DMs, the inbound context sets `To` as `user:{aadObjectId}`. When the `send` tool later\\nresolves the target via `resolveMSTeamsSendContext`, it calls `findByUserId` in the conversation\\nstore, which iterates all stored conversations and returns the **first** entry matching the\\nuser\\u0026#39;s AAD object ID or Bot Framework ID — with no awareness of conversation type or recency.\\n\\nSince `Object.entries()` iteration order depends on insertion order in the JSON store, the\\nresult is non-deterministic from the user\\u0026#39;s perspective: if the channel/group conversation\\nwas stored before the personal DM, the proactive message is delivered there instead.\\n\\nBoth the filesystem store (`conversation-store-fs.ts`) and the in-memory store\\n(`conversation-store-memory.ts`) share this behavior.\\n\\n## Solution\\n\\nUpdate `findByUserId` in both store implementations to collect **all** matching entries for a\\nuser, then apply a preference:\\n\\n1. **Prefer `personal` (1:1) conversations** — when a user lookup is performed (typically for\\n   DM-initiated proactive sends), the personal conversation is the semantically correct target.\\n2. **Fall back deterministically** — when no personal conversation exists, the fs store returns\\n   the most recently seen entry (by `lastSeenAt` timestamp, which already exists in the\\n   persisted data), and the memory store returns the first match.\\n\\nThis approach was chosen over changing the `To` format (Option 2 in the issue) or threading\\nsession context (Option 3/4) because:\\n\\n- It fixes the bug at the source (`findByUserId`) without changing the inbound context format,\\n  avoiding downstream breakage in code paths that parse `user:` prefix for DM detection.\\n- It leverages the `conversationType` field already stored in every conversation reference.\\n- It fixes **all** callers of `findByUserId`, not just the DM inbound path.\\n- The `lastSeenAt` field already exists in the fs store data, so no schema changes are needed.\\n\\n## Changed files\\n\\n| File |
